The time of the midpoint of the sample is used to designate the sample as day or night. Its important because the CPR sample is at a fixed depth, but some zooplankton migrate upwards at night, therefore some taxa are only sampled at night. For some statistics you will need to know the proportion of day versus night samples in a particular region and time frame. "	df35d.195.12	1	3	"date  Position, date and time information of the sample is taken from ship’s log information and refers to the midpoint of the 18.5 km sample. Zooplankton counts are recorded for all species and specimen types in each sample. CPR sample analysis is reported for two zooplankton stages: ""eyecount"" and ""traverse"". ""Eyecount""= zooplankton larger than 2mm; whole sample is checked by eye for presence of species, which are then removed from the sample to be identified under the microscope. ""Traverse""= zooplankton smaller than 2mm; sub sample under lower magnification; traverse of the sample is made by microscope, and all individuals are counted. "	df35d.195.12	1	8	planktonType  Indicates phyoplankton or zooplankton being analyzed in the sample 	df35d.195.12	1	9	"NEWSpeciesName Revised taxonomic name The current revised taxonomic name. Colour= 0, 1, 2, 3 (relates to green colour of the mesh) and phytoplankton= 1-10 (number of fields of view divided by two and expressed as an integer). Sometimes an organism is too rare to be counted in its correct analysis stage but is seen in a subsequent analysis stage. Titer testing employs serial dilution to obtain approximate quantitative information from an analytical procedure that inherently only evaluates as positive or negative. The titer corresponds to the highest dilution factor that still yields a positive reading. For example, positive readings in the first 8 serial twofold dilutions translate into a titer of 1:256 (i.e., 2−8). Titers are sometimes expressed by the denominator only, for example 1:256 is written 256."	doi:10.5063/F1QJ7F7N	2	7	"testResult  Test result code (text), followed by the two-digit year in some cases. In kg. kilogram	doi:10.5063/F1TB14T4	1	15	Notes  Notes from capture event 	doi:10.5063/F1TB14T4	1	16	"fattyAcid  Fatty acid signature. A fatty acid is a carboxylic acid with a long aliphatic (carbon chain) tail which is either saturated (no double bonds between carbon pairs) or unsaturated (at least one double bond between carbon pairs). In the naming of fatty acids, lipid numbers take the form C:D, where C is the number of carbon atoms in the fatty acid chain and D is the number of double bonds in the fatty acid (if more than one, the double bonds are assumed to be interrupted by CH2 units, i.e., at intervals of 3 carbon atoms along the chain). This notation can be ambiguous, as some different fatty acids can have the same numbers. n−x nomenclature both provides names for individual compounds and classifies them by their likely biosynthetic properties in animals. A double bond is located on the xth carbon–carbon bond, counting from the terminal methyl carbon (designated as n toward the carbonyl carbon. For example: linolenic acid is written as 18:2 n-6, this means that there are 18 carbons in the fatty acid chain and there are 2 double bonds, with the first double bond occurring 6 carbons from the methyl end (between carbons 6 and 7) and the second would be at the 9th carbon (between carbons 9 and 10).  Here is a drawing of the chemical structure for linolenic acid (18:2 n-6) CH3-CH2-CH2-CH2-CH2-CH=CH-CH2-CH=CH-CH2-CH2-CH2-CH2-CH2-CH2-CH2-COOH. i and ai stands for iso and anteiso, which are branched chain fatty acids, me stands for fatty acids that contain a methyl group, d stands for deoxy, and represents fatty acids with less oxygen atoms than normal. "	doi:10.5063/F1TB14T4	1	17	amount  The amount represents each fatty acid's (FA's) relative abundance among all the FA's quantified for that sample dimensionless	doi:10.5063/F1TB14T4	2	1	RecordNo  Sequential record number number	doi:10.5063/F1TB14T4	2	2	LabCode  No information 	doi:10.5063/F1TB14T4	2	3	CommonName  Common name of prey sampled 	doi:10.5063/F1TB14T4	2	4	SpeciesName  Genus/species of prey sampled 	doi:10.5063/F1TB14T4	2	5	CollLocation  Location of sample collection 	doi:10.5063/F1TB14T4	2	6	"Area  Area of sample collection (e.g. Prince William Sound, Southeast Alaska, Kodiak) "	doi:10.5063/F1TB14T4	2	7	"SubArea  breakdown of the area into regions (e.g. North, South, Central, Northwest) "	doi:10.5063/F1TB14T4	2	8	CollMonth  Month of sample collection number	doi:10.5063/F1TB14T4	2	9	CollYear  Year of sample collection 	doi:10.5063/F1TB14T4	2	10	"Length_cm  Length of prey sampled, in centimeters centimeter"	doi:10.5063/F1TB14T4	2	11	Mass_g  Mass of prey sampled in grams gram	doi:10.5063/F1TB14T4	2	12	Lipid  lipid content; percentage of wet weight. dimensionless	doi:10.5063/F1TB14T4	2	13	Comments1  comments 	doi:10.5063/F1TB14T4	2	14	Comments2  comments 	doi:10.5063/F1TB14T4	2	15	"fattyAcid  Fatty acid signature.
